## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox CSS calc() Value Overflow

## Your Task

Firefox crashes when processing CSS calc() with extreme values. Find the C++ source files in mozilla/gecko-dev that (1) parse CSS calc() expressions and (2) handle numeric overflow during calc() value resolution.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

67-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've identified and documented the C++ and Rust source files in Firefox that handle CSS calc() parsing and numeric overflow. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Files Identified

**Primary Files:**
1. **servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs** - Generic calc node implementation with the critical `resolve_internal()` method (lines 928-1184) that evaluates calc() expressions
2. **servo/components/style/values/specified/calc.rs** - Parses CSS calc() expressions into AST structure
3. **servo/components/style/values/computed/length_percentage.rs** - CalcLengthPercentage struct with the `resolve()` method (lines 991-1008)
4. **servo/ports/geckolib/glue.rs** - FFI bridge function `Servo_ResolveCalcLengthPercentage()` that connects Rust to C++
5. **layout/style/ServoStyleConstsInlines.h** - C++ inline method `StyleCalcLengthPercentage::ResolveToCSSPixels()`

## Root Cause

The vulnerability occurs in the `resolve_internal()` method in **servo/components/style/values/generics/calc.rs**, specifically in operations that perform unchecked floating-point arithmetic:

- **Line 1105-1107**: `round()` function with extreme step values
- **Line 1153**: Hypot calculation squaring values with `v.powi(2)` 
- **Line 1165**: Accumulating squared values `v + child_value.powi(2)`

These operations with extreme CSS calc() values (near f32::MAX ≈ 3.4e38) cause overflow before the clamping logic can take effect, resulting in Firefox crashes.

The answer file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol names, and call chain information.
